  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8e98834b-bea1-4dbb-800c-6ee38f1d771e'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText3406393582350454035" style="display:none">A century has passed since the heroic defence of Dros Delnoch. But the people of the Drenai face a new terror: a mad emperor kept in power by two forces of unsurpassed evil. The Joinings are werebeasts of awesome power. The Dark Templars are warrior-priests whose fighting skills are without equal. Against them, the Drenai face certain defeat.<br /><br />One man, an outsider hated by the Drenai for his Nadir blood, and despised by the Nadir for his Drenai ancestry, sets out to bring down the emperor. He is one man against the armies of chaos.<br /><br />He is Tenaka Khan - the Prince of Shadows.</span>

<div id="bookReviews">
  




  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2305679740" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2305679740" />
    <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries"><img alt="Mayim de Vries" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560508357p2/50424456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2305679740?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mayim de Vries" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries">Mayim de Vries</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2305679740" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12420201492669892132"><i>"For centuries the Drenai have turned back enemies who would have done this to our land. And now we do it ourselves."</i><br/><br/><b>If you loved <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1577771334' rel='nofollow noopener'>Legend</a>, chances are huge that you will love the King Beyond the Gate for it does follow the same pattern. Two people on the margins of life meet and fall madly in love. One of them has violet eyes. Together they take on a hopeless cause. The battle is fought on two planes, the physical and the spiritual one. There are roses.</b><br/><br/>King Beyond the Gate is the second volume of</span>
  <span id="freeText12420201492669892132" style="display:none"><i>"For centuries the Drenai have turned back enemies who would have done this to our land. And now we do it ourselves."</i><br /><br /><b>If you loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1577771334" rel="nofollow noopener">Legend</a>, chances are huge that you will love the King Beyond the Gate for it does follow the same pattern. Two people on the margins of life meet and fall madly in love. One of them has violet eyes. Together they take on a hopeless cause. The battle is fought on two planes, the physical and the spiritual one. There are roses.</b><br /><br />King Beyond the Gate is the second volume of the Drenai saga. The action takes place 100 years after the events described in the Legend. The Drenai land was taken over by usurper Ceska, who created an army of mutants called Joinings. The tyrant is aided by the evil equivalent of the Thirty called Black Templars. The land is torn apart by civil war.<br /><br />There are <b>many similarities and analogies between the events and characters</b>, that some of the protagonists might look like crude copycats. The second thing you will notice is that <b>in Gemmell’s land time practically stands still</b>. For over one hundred years, there has been practically no progress. The only development is that the researchers there were able to re-start the complicated machines of the mysterious Elders, used to create hybrids between humans and animals.<br /><br />On the one hand, the Author weaves in <b>a few interesting threads</b>, such as the Dragon Legion, which is an elite Drenai unit, or the horrifying Joinings. There are also <b>elements that were a strong point in the previous volume in the series: valour, epic fights, heroic deeds</b>.<br /><br />And yet, <b>I missed something. Maybe a hero who would "pull off" the whole thing?</b> In the Legend we have the Earl of Bronze or Druss - men who seemed larger than life itself, who inspired to fight, encouraged, and attracted others. I have the impression that in the "King Beyond the Gate" this very strong personality is missing. Who's supposed to be the one? Tenaka, half-Nadir, half-Drenai, who does not know himself where he actually belongs? Ananais, a golden warrior who, along with the terrible wound he receives in battle, loses faith in himself? Decado, who, leading the Thirty warrior monks, cannot fully gain their love and loyalty, even if he has their obedience? Or maybe Scaler, who tries so hard to become the Prince of the Bronze, even if he only pretends to be such figure? Also, the female protagonists are not that interesting either.<br /><br /><b>Maybe Mr Gemmell wanted to write a novel where heroes would not be perfect, statuesque ideals. Maybe he wanted to create persuasive characters who would not be black and white, but represent different shades of grey instead.</b> I think it went well, but it also had one serious effect: I could not quite like any of them. And I don’t think anyone is memorable enough to make the book special.<br /><br /><b>I think you can safely skip this volume in a series that is long enough to offer you other, more entertaining books.</b><br /><br />---<br />Also in The Drenai Saga: <br /><br />1. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1577771334" rel="nofollow noopener">Legend</a> ★★★★★ <br />3. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2336920559" rel="nofollow noopener">Waylander</a> ★★★☆☆<br />4. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2372503520" rel="nofollow noopener">Quest for Lost Heroes</a> ★★★★☆<br />5. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2407425852" rel="nofollow noopener">In the Realm of the Wolf</a> ★★★☆☆<br />6. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2431984941?type=review#rating_170330840" rel="nofollow noopener">The First Chronicles of Druss the Legend</a> ★★★★☆<br />7. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2470949369" rel="nofollow noopener">The Legend of Deathwalker</a> ★★★★☆<br />8. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2517328446?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Winter Warriors</a> ★★★☆☆<br />9. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2621547766" rel="nofollow noopener">Hero in the Shadows</a> ★★★★★<br />10. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2622814693?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">White Wolf</a> ★★☆☆☆<br />11. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2625913227?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Swords of Night and Day</a> ★☆☆☆☆</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11760258067268262022">The King Beyond the Gate (The Drenai Saga #2), David Gemmell<br/>The King Beyond The Gate is a fantasy novel by British writer David Gemmell. It was published in 1985. It was the second book published by Gemmell, after Legend, published a year earlier. The book is set in the same fictional world as Legend, that of the Drenai, but is not a sequel in the usual sense as the events of the two books take place around a century apart. Thus the main protagonists of Legend are long since dead and play little</span>
  <span id="freeText11760258067268262022" style="display:none">The King Beyond the Gate (The Drenai Saga #2), David Gemmell<br />The King Beyond The Gate is a fantasy novel by British writer David Gemmell. It was published in 1985. It was the second book published by Gemmell, after Legend, published a year earlier. The book is set in the same fictional world as Legend, that of the Drenai, but is not a sequel in the usual sense as the events of the two books take place around a century apart. Thus the main protagonists of Legend are long since dead and play little part in The King Beyond the Gate, other than passing mentions. This set a precedent for the entire Drenai series, in which very few characters appear in more than one novel, the gaps between novels sometimes running to centuries, giving a more epic, historical flavour to the series.<br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: ماه دسامبر سال 2010 میلادی<br />عنوان: پادشاه آنسوی دروازه؛ نویسنده: دیوید گمل؛ مترجم: سهیلا فرزین نژاد؛ تهران، کتابسرای تندیس، 1389، در 471 ص؛ شابک: 9789648944631؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان انگلیسی قرن 20 م<br />داستانی گیرا و پر کشش است، در دنیای درنای میگذرد، اما ادامه اسطوره نیست، چند بار خوانده ام؛ بهتر است خود بخوانید. ا. شربیانی</span>
  <a data-text-id="11760258067268262022" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer10666523948785844352">This was extremely disappointing, it was barely an average read. What made it worse was that the first book was amazing, I really loved that and gave it five stars while this was a struggle. The only reason why I didn't dnf this was that it was a short book, just 300+ pages, if it was longer I know I would not have finished it.<br/><br/>This book has way too many flaws, here are a few. The events here happened like a hundred years after book one, so they are all new characters, two of the protagonists are</span>
  <span id="freeText10666523948785844352" style="display:none">This was extremely disappointing, it was barely an average read. What made it worse was that the first book was amazing, I really loved that and gave it five stars while this was a struggle. The only reason why I didn't dnf this was that it was a short book, just 300+ pages, if it was longer I know I would not have finished it.<br /><br />This book has way too many flaws, here are a few. The events here happened like a hundred years after book one, so they are all new characters, two of the protagonists are the progeny of Rek and the Nadir warlord. Not much was said about what happened within the 100 years period. <br /><br />Presently a tyrant known as Ceska is now ruling Drenai, having killed the original rulers and displaced the heir. He meld humans and animals together to make super soldiers, they are very hard to kill.<br /><br />Tenaka Khan is a result of a union between a Nadir and Drenai, both sides don't like him because of his other half. He knows this, he is also a warrior feared by both sides. His character like all the others wasn't well developed.<br /><br />Annaias is his friend who is vain but somewhat noble. Due to some incident he is missing the skin on his face.<br /><br />Renya is a female character that is not completely human, I liked her at first but at last I couldn't care less.<br /><br />There were other cool characters in this like Valtaya, Pagan, Lake and many others.<br /><br />This book has so much potential to be good but the writing was terrible and the POV shift was too sparodic. Instead of fast paced everything was rushed, I felt like I was reading a fast forwarded book. The world building and fight scenes were the only thing in this book that was well depicted. The plot would have been better if the author had taken time to portray the story well. Do not even get me started on the insta love.</span>

        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer533980614" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9156050206189239518">I think the blurb on my edition's cover gave the best description of the book, "The greatest army of the Drenai was dead to a man - and that man sought revenge..." There is almost nothing more to say. The Drenai nation is under the rule of a tyrant who can create a mutants/werewolves/werebears, etc. to support his oppression of people. A former general of Drenai army choose not to participate in the war that led to the tyrant's rise to power. Now that his army is gone, and the terror stalks the </span>
  <span id="freeText9156050206189239518" style="display:none">I think the blurb on my edition's cover gave the best description of the book, "The greatest army of the Drenai was dead to a man - and that man sought revenge..." There is almost nothing more to say. The Drenai nation is under the rule of a tyrant who can create a mutants/werewolves/werebears, etc. to support his oppression of people. A former general of Drenai army choose not to participate in the war that led to the tyrant's rise to power. Now that his army is gone, and the terror stalks the land unopposed - the general has really nothing to lose, but he is only one man.<br /><br />I cannot help but to compare this book to the first one in the series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/618177.Legend__Drenai_Saga___1_" title="Legend (Drenai Saga, #1) by David Gemmell" rel="nofollow noopener">Legend</a>. The plot resembles the one of the first book, as well as characters: I could actually find which characters from the second book correspond to the ones of the first book, and vice versa. Having said that, the characters from this book are much more developed and interesting. On the other hand, Druss the Legend alone carried the first book and there was nobody equal to him in this one. <br /><br />I was sure the book is worth 3 stars up until the end, but it was so powerful and unexpected that I did not hesitate to raise it. This is in sharp contrast to forced happy end of the Legend. In this instance it was clear that the quality of writing improved a lot. </span>

    <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar"><img alt="Dirk Grobbelaar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545117991p2/3102740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/86932897?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dirk Grobbelaar" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar">Dirk Grobbelaar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=must-read-in-2020">must-read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer86932897" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1625010785713402880"><br/><i>'How many of you are there?'<br/>'One hundred only. But judge us not by our number. Rather, watch the numbers of dead we leave behind us.'</i><br/><br/>Gemmell was a master at this kind of thing: rousing heroic fantasy with larger-than-life, but flawed, characters (often past their prime) in an interesting setting. The Drenai books are actually quite remarkable. The writing is to the point, but very effective, and Gemmell’s action sequences are the stuff of Legend (ho ho). <br/><br/><i>Ahead, like dark demons out of the past, </i></span>
  <span id="freeText1625010785713402880" style="display:none"><br /><i>'How many of you are there?'<br />'One hundred only. But judge us not by our number. Rather, watch the numbers of dead we leave behind us.'</i><br /><br />Gemmell was a master at this kind of thing: rousing heroic fantasy with larger-than-life, but flawed, characters (often past their prime) in an interesting setting. The Drenai books are actually quite remarkable. The writing is to the point, but very effective, and Gemmell’s action sequences are the stuff of Legend (ho ho). <br /><br /><i>Ahead, like dark demons out of the past, twenty riders waited in a line. They sat their horses immobile, black cloaks flapping in the breeze.</i><br /><br />I found the whole affair very atmospheric and brimming with old-school cool. Even the magic system is interesting, with some nods to mysticism thrown into the sorcerous mix (such as the source priests battling the dark templars on the spirit plane). <br /><br /><i>‘We are nature's killers and we have great appetites for it. Even the heroes we remember show our love of war. Druss, the greatest killing machine of all time - it is his image you stare upon in the council chamber.'</i><br /><br />The philosophical aspects of the story are introduced in a non-intrusive way that never bogs the story down. Even though the focus is squarely on bloodshed, there are some interesting questions raised regarding the need for violence and the nature of those that perpetuate it.<br /><br />This story takes place around a century after the battle at Dros Delnoch, so there are some references to Druss the Legend and the Earl of Bronze. Even so, the Drenai books can easily be read as standalone novels.<br /><br />In conclusion: a very good heroic fantasy tale by a master of the genre. <br /><br /><i>He moved to a set of armour placed to the right of the rest and his hand reached down to curl round the ivory hilt. With one smooth movement he swept the blade into the air, his muscles pulsing with the thrill of the weapon. Its blade was silver steel and razor-sharp, and the balance was perfection.</i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1625010785713402880" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_872435007" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/872435007" />
    <a title="Nate" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6803829-nate"><img alt="Nate" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413944642p2/6803829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/872435007?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nate" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nate" href="/user/show/6803829-nate">Nate</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6803829-nate?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer872435007" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12969297666417709239">The perpetually-imperiled nation of the Drenai is under attack once more, not by the Nadir hordes of the northern steppes, but by their own government under the tyrant Ceska. Attentive readers of the awesome <i>Legend</i>, which dealt with the First Nadir War, are obviously gonna be confused by Gemmell's almost-immediate mention of the Second Nadir War in between the first and second books. Well, turns out, in the wake of the events in <i>Legend</i>, the Drenai formed a badass ultra-elite regiment called the </span>
  <span id="freeText12969297666417709239" style="display:none">The perpetually-imperiled nation of the Drenai is under attack once more, not by the Nadir hordes of the northern steppes, but by their own government under the tyrant Ceska. Attentive readers of the awesome <i>Legend</i>, which dealt with the First Nadir War, are obviously gonna be confused by Gemmell's almost-immediate mention of the Second Nadir War in between the first and second books. Well, turns out, in the wake of the events in <i>Legend</i>, the Drenai formed a badass ultra-elite regiment called the Dragon and they were instrumental in repelling a second Nadir invasion. One of the dudes in that regiment was a Drenai/Nadir half-blood dude named Tenaka Khan...and now he is the last of the Dragon to stand against the newly-risen tyrant Ceska, who now controls the Drenai Nation with a bloody iron fist. Obviously there's a surplus of ass to get kicked, and Tenaka seems to be the only one to do it. Overall this story is a little bigger than the siege of Dros Delnoch from the first book but it's hardly sweeping (thank the Old Gods and the New...I just finished Christian Cameron's <i>The Fell Sword</i> and it was a bit of a strain (although a sublime one, and I will hopefully get to reviewing it soon. In the meantime, start reading those books motherfuckers.)<br /><br />Gemmell was not about (and I don't think really cared about) extensive and detailed complex worldbuilding or unique, complex plots but the stories have been consistently and thoroughly fun so far. The pretty-low magic content comes from the humorously Force-like "Source" which even has its own Jedi-type superpowered knights called the Thirty with their own dark, chaotic counterparts to combat and stuff like that. There's also some dark machine-made man-beast monstrous hybrids named Joinings...but that's about it. The basic idea is good shit. It skips the detailed politicking, traveling and worldbuilding and magic systems of the usual fantasy and just goes right to the moments where nations are just gonna fucking duke it out, with guaranteed constant badassery and well-crafted set pieces. It's not deep stuff by any means, it's just <i>good</i>. It's like restaurants. You (probably) try new places, but sometimes you just wanna go a place where you know what you're gonna get and that it's gonna be good shit.<br /><br />Gemmell's pretty good with characters...I mean, you're not gonna find a startlingly realistic and deep human being in these pages but the man did come up with Druss the fucking Legend, so you have to give him some credit. He's just good at coming up with tortured yet heroic badasses, and there's a ton in this book; Tenaka Khan, unerringly deadly swordsman and outcast from two warring nations; Ananais the Golden, a once-handsome leader of men who was horribly disfigured and still maintains minimum-level Gemmell badassery content by wearing a creepy mask; Decado the Ice Killer, an unstoppable force of death who has given up the sword in exchange for peaceful living with the Thirty; and Rayvan, the brave rebel general and leader of imperiled refugees who worries deeply for her soldier sons. They have passionate yet unrealistic doomed love stories, angst over skeletons in their closets and hero it the fuck up with abandon, slaying hordes of enemies in desperate battles every chance they get. One or two might buy the farm over the course of the story, but you know it's gonna be in an utterly badass and heroic way, so it's all good. It's not like some dark "gonna swallow a bottle of pills because I just finished <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i>A Storm of Swords</i>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> fantasy death.<br /><br />There's just not a lot to complain about. It's an obvious formula, but it's a good one. There's just some formulas you like and want to return to frequently and you don't want them fucked with. That's the kind of writer Gemmell was. They may not get the praise from any group of critical luminaries but they probably don't care and their fans don't either. The dialogue can be stilted and goofy, but occasionally Gemmell will hit upon some interesting insight in the characters' differing philosophy. His prose is direct and easy as hell to read but doesn't come off crude or rudimentary. The books aren't long and there's no real challenge to keeping track of setting, characters, or plot. It's just basic shit--reluctant heroes fight in epic wars between varying factions. I really don't mean any of this to sound like any kind of backhanded compliment--there are dense and complex fantasies high and low and then there are just faith-in-humanity reaffirming stories of dudes (and Gemmell does of course have his share of powerful, effective, dangerous and heroic women...I actually think despite the traditional vibe his stories were pretty progressive, with the paradoxically-secular-feeling Source and the egalitarianism towards gay characters, which is awesome!) doing heroic shit like it's just going down the block to get something to eat. Gemmell seems to be a master of the latter. It's weird, because I was not bowled over by his first Troy story...should probably revisit those.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12969297666417709239" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2287575445" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2287575445" />
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66331236-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568827728p2/66331236.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2287575445?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/66331236-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2287575445" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14417613383342532772"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1521787167i/25259382._SY540_.jpg' width='840' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>I was super nervous when I started The King Beyond The Gate. You see, I read this book 10 years ago and the hero, Tenaka Khan was my first experience of a larger than life warrior. I absolutely loved him. So I had all these expectations and I started it with the worry, “Would this book be as amazing as it’d been the first time?” When I read it the first time, I was much younger and I worried that my older self wouldn’t be as impressed by Tenaka Khan as my younger self had been. I didn’t want a b</span>
  <span id="freeText14417613383342532772" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1521787167i/25259382._SY540_.jpg" width="840" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I was super nervous when I started The King Beyond The Gate. You see, I read this book 10 years ago and the hero, Tenaka Khan was my first experience of a larger than life warrior. I absolutely loved him. So I had all these expectations and I started it with the worry, “Would this book be as amazing as it’d been the first time?” When I read it the first time, I was much younger and I worried that my older self wouldn’t be as impressed by Tenaka Khan as my younger self had been. I didn’t want a bitter disillusionment.<br><br>TKBTG follows the life of Tenaka Khan, born half-Drenai, half-Nadir, shunned by both. It was hard for him to live on the brink of two worlds, to be hated by both because of his mixed blood. I felt such empathy for Tenaka Khan. In spite of his mixed blood though, I was glad that he had friends who respected him and a mother who loved him.<br><br>Then he met Renya. Drenai and a Joining to boot. She was spectacular, especially one particular scene where she was the one who had to save <i>him</i>, the fearless warrior Tenaka Khan. 😉<br><br><i>“Where Tenaka Khan walked, there would be Renya. He was unaware of it as yet. But he would learn.”</i> Lol. I kept thinking, you go, girl!<br><br>She fell for him and then she wanted to change him. That didn’t sit well with me, maybe because I did the same. Throughout reading the story, I started to be a bit disappointed in Tenaka Khan. (Yes, I love his name lol.) You see, he wasn’t the flawless hero I’d imagined him to be all those years ago. In typical David Gemmell fashion, he was an anti-hero, with his flaws and issues, like Renya found out. I read his story through rose-colored glasses ten years ago and now I was seeing the reality and boy, was it a revelation in disbelief!<br><br>But he was still a decent man and he changed the fate of the Nadir by uniting all the tribes as one nation. I couldn’t expect him to be both Drenai and the Great Khan of the Nadir. His destiny was to rule the Nadir and they needed him.<br><br>Once I accepted that, I enjoyed the story a lot more. Add in the dry wit – there were scenes which were so funny at times which I didn’t expect that I laughed out loud – and the plot was pretty good. I don’t know why Tenaka Khan got such a grip on my heart but he still had it.<br><br><a href="https://nomadicworlds.wordpress.com/2018/03/23/book-review-the-king-beyond-the-gate-david-gemmell/" rel="nofollow noopener">Posted on Blog</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14417613383342532772" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345379054" href="/book/show/544619.The_King_Beyond_the_Gate">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=sword-sorcery">sword-sorcery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=2fiction">2fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=1paper">1paper</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1470312819" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11668571811583770286">I expected this to fill in the holes in Druss' saga, but it was set after his time. He was a legendary hero to aspire to. It was a good S&S tale. I liked it at least as much as the first book. There were a lot of conflicted characters, none perfectly good or bad. No unicorns farting rainbows - some things just don't work out & good characters die.<br/><br/>This isn't a deep complex series, though. That is not a criticism, just an observation. Gemmell just shows us the bit of the world we need, although th</span>
  <span id="freeText11668571811583770286" style="display:none">I expected this to fill in the holes in Druss' saga, but it was set after his time. He was a legendary hero to aspire to. It was a good S&amp;S tale. I liked it at least as much as the first book. There were a lot of conflicted characters, none perfectly good or bad. No unicorns farting rainbows - some things just don't work out &amp; good characters die.<br /><br />This isn't a deep complex series, though. That is not a criticism, just an observation. Gemmell just shows us the bit of the world we need, although there are hints of a larger world &amp; there is certainly room for other books. While he has obviously devised a rich world, his prose is lean &amp; the story is straight forward. I appreciated that.<br /><br />The magic isn't too obtrusive, although any deus ex machina is neatly attributed to The Source, a sort of Fate. Thankfully, that's used sparingly &amp; pretty well. I only really questioned it once &amp; then had to chuckle when I realized just how clever he'd been. Well played! <br /><br />I have a few more of these books, but think that's enough for now. I'm not sure when I got them nor why they wound up in my regular shelves instead of my TBR shelf. That's disturbing. My book memory is slipping. Anyway, I look forward to reading more in this series.</span>

<div id="review_255901667" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/255901667" />
    <a title="Jayaprakash Satyamurthy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1497559-jayaprakash-satyamurthy"><img alt="Jayaprakash Satyamurthy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517076488p2/1497559.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/255901667?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jayaprakash Satyamurthy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jayaprakash Satyamurthy" href="/user/show/1497559-jayaprakash-satyamurthy">Jayaprakash Satyamurthy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345379054" href="/book/show/544619.The_King_Beyond_the_Gate">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1497559-jayaprakash-satyamurthy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer255901667" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14366556831132612081">I was very ready to be disappointed by this novel; second of a series as well as one of the first few Gemmells I've read. There were times when it seemed like the story was a little too similar to Legend; but for the most part this resolved into the fact that it was really the same conflict, a generation later. I also feared that the romantic interests in the novel would see Gemmell starting to emulate that other David, Eddings, in the cozy, cloying way he pairs off members of his party of adven</span>
  <span id="freeText14366556831132612081" style="display:none">I was very ready to be disappointed by this novel; second of a series as well as one of the first few Gemmells I've read. There were times when it seemed like the story was a little too similar to Legend; but for the most part this resolved into the fact that it was really the same conflict, a generation later. I also feared that the romantic interests in the novel would see Gemmell starting to emulate that other David, Eddings, in the cozy, cloying way he pairs off members of his party of adventurers, but our David here has a more complex understanding of human nature even if his emotional scenes are not the most sophisticated. <br /><br />Oh but the heroics. Once again there were scenes of heroism on large and small stages, physical, mental and spiritual and always against the odds. Stirring scenes of sacrifice, camaraderie and loyalty. Gemmell wrote heroic fantasy and his conception of heroism was robust, unapologetic and downright inspiring. And once again, martial highlights are supported by equally effective magical elements and a cast of rugged, endearing characters which is if anything even more varied and memorable than the last time around (although no one quite reaches the archetypal level of Druss). Honest, effective entertainment that wears its heart on its sleeve. I can think of worse ways to spend my time. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14366556831132612081" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

"No more David Gemmell Books . . . sad . . . " If you are a fan of classic fantasy and haven't read anything by him you're missing out. <div id="review_408279471" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/408279471" />
    <a title="Max" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5756118-max"><img alt="Max" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1334262755p2/5756118.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/408279471?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Max" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Max" href="/user/show/5756118-max">Max</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345379054" href="/book/show/544619.The_King_Beyond_the_Gate">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5756118-max?shelf=scifi-fantasy">scifi-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer408279471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13979885382366749915">David Gemmell is one of my favorite authors of all time, but this book fell a little short. The biggest shortfall is that it is very similar to <i>Legend</i>, but it's not as good. All of the major elements that made <i>Legend</i> one of my favorite books are there, but they just aren't pulled off as well. The characters aren't as deep. The story isn't as engaging. The inspiration isn't as inspirational. The menace isn't as menacing. The battles aren't as awe-inspiring. None of these things would normally be </span>
  <span id="freeText13979885382366749915" style="display:none">David Gemmell is one of my favorite authors of all time, but this book fell a little short. The biggest shortfall is that it is very similar to <i>Legend</i>, but it's not as good. All of the major elements that made <i>Legend</i> one of my favorite books are there, but they just aren't pulled off as well. The characters aren't as deep. The story isn't as engaging. The inspiration isn't as inspirational. The menace isn't as menacing. The battles aren't as awe-inspiring. None of these things would normally be too big of a deal because it's nearly impossible to match the greatness of those same elements in <i>Legend</i>. The issue is that the stories are so similar that you can't help but compare.<br /><br />It's still a good story and well worth the read, but I would rank it towards the bottom of the Drenai series. Other books like <i>Waylander</i> and <i>Quest for Lost Heroes</i> are better reads. It's definitely something that you should read, but the great part about the Drenai series is that you don't need to read them in order. Therefore, you can read this one towards the end and distance it from <i>Legend</i> to a certain extent.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13979885382366749915" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34550725-alfred-haplo?shelf=sf-fantasy-mytho">sf-fantasy-mytho</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34550725-alfred-haplo?shelf=1970-to-1999">1970-to-1999</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2281699403" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6186286303491089198">A century after <i>Legend</i>, the battles continue in <i>The King Beyond the Gate</i>*. A cruel ruler and his abominations rise within Drenai, whilst the Nadir keep at bay in tense truce. A call to aid brings home old warriors to fight in vain, but some calls lay unheeded by those who have long left that life of death. Death, as always, has other plans. <br/><br/>By the end, blood will flow thick and fast but so will love and courage. They go hand in hand, it appears, with one preceding the other in an endless loop. <i>T</i></span>
  <span id="freeText6186286303491089198" style="display:none">A century after <i>Legend</i>, the battles continue in <i>The King Beyond the Gate</i>*. A cruel ruler and his abominations rise within Drenai, whilst the Nadir keep at bay in tense truce. A call to aid brings home old warriors to fight in vain, but some calls lay unheeded by those who have long left that life of death. Death, as always, has other plans. <br /><br />By the end, blood will flow thick and fast but so will love and courage. They go hand in hand, it appears, with one preceding the other in an endless loop. <i>TKBtGate</i> brings us back into the loop of Gemmell’s world of wars and warriors, brothers and brotherhood, with the women standing alongside as lovers and leaders. If the legendary Druss was an atomic bomb who decimated all at ground zero in <i>Legend</i>, then the protagonists in <i>TKBtGate</i> are shockwaves rippling from the core. Their heroism is no less powerful, but their heroics a softer thunder. <br /><br />As story has it, <i>Legend</i> was written at a time when Gemmell was battling cancer **. He had created the mighty Druss, whose invincibility became a mantra of hope over hopelessness. The kind of character who fights and inspires until death, but till then, he keeps fighting and keeps inspiring. This element continues to ring true in <i>TKBtGate</i> where in my obfuscated view, I see the collective heroes of Tenaka, Ananais, Rayvan and Decado ** as Druss deconstructed, respectively as The Strategist, The General, The Heart and The Killer. <br /><br />These protagonists, perhaps each as a facet of Druss, develop more individually here. One of my chief dissatisfaction with <i>Legend</i> was in how Druss is presented wholesale, whereas <i>TKBtGate</i> allows us to examine each person slightly more thoroughly as we learn a bit more of each one. And because we do that, we see their naivete, their vanity, their ambitions more clearly. We get to reconsider if our heroes are truly heroes, or just heroic at that point in time. <br /><br />Those are not the only heroes, as there seem to be many more in this novel. The Thirty and Earl of Bronze resurrect in spirit if not in form, with a barbaric King joining the fray. What makes the heroes in <i>TKBtGate</i> distinct from many of today’s fantasy heroes is not just how fractured they are, but in how fractured they stay. Redemption is sometimes earned by death, which is not only brave of these characters to embrace, but also of the author. Kill them all, if not today, then another day but die they all will. <br /><br />For me, reading Gemmell is like witnessing a battlefield grave. I am moved in a philosophical way by the cause and the massive casualty, but unmoved emotionally for lack of a personal connection. In a sense, you read stories like <i>Legend</i> and <i>TKBtGate</i> for those big moments of valor and sacrifice, the kinds that stab you in the heart and make you cry because you know people have to die in order for others or themselves to be free. But my feelings, though, never soared.<br /><br />So far, based on my two Gemmells, neither depth nor nuance is a forte. A large cast with so many moving parts cannot be crammed into 300+ pages without short-cuts. The formidable Dragon Army is a cursory mention only to introduce certain warriors, and the mysterious Machines that morph beasts with men seemed sufficient to explain the legionnaire of evil Joinings. Pivotal events happen in quick time, particularly with relationships where easily love surrenders, friendship forgives and faith submits. If you can ignore these nagging holes and economical characterization, then boy oh boy, what a thrilling read this is. <br /><br />If <i>Legend</i> was originally written without an end in mind **, then clearly <i>TKBtGate</i> is the opposite. The story appears to move in concentric circle from afar and purposefully spirals faster and closer to the climactic battle at the end, where magic and magical beings, foes and friends, must once again clash for victory, but this time not of territory but of souls. <br /><br />I love the epilogues at the end of each novel, for they give me closure. The conclusion of <i>TKBtGate</i> is satisfying enough to move on without ever needing a re-read but also tantalizing enough for a return to this world with a sense of continuation, of knowing exactly what to expect from Gemmell. <br /><br /><i>TKBtGate</i> is not a better or worse novel than <i>Legend</i>, but it is complementary where it should be and supplemental where it can. The same 3.5 star rating applies, rounded up.<br /><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user_status/show/160443421" rel="nofollow noopener"> Spillover thoughts here</a>. <br /><br /><br />[* The Drenai Saga: <i>Legend</i> #1, <i>The King Beyond the Gate</i> #2 and several other standalone books.<br /><br />** Thank you, Wastrel, for that extra bit of information]</span>
  <a data-text-id="6186286303491089198" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText18375592955034105832" style="display:none">I finally managed to drag myself to the finish line on this. That it took me this long for such a short book is insane. If I didn't need this book for a couple of reading challenges I probably would've dropped this. I liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/618177.Legend__The_Drenai_Saga___1_" title="Legend (The Drenai Saga, #1) by David Gemmell" rel="nofollow noopener">Legend</a> better. This felt pretty much like a rehash of Legend's plot. While the book had some good, non-dialogue lines most of the actual dialogue between characters felt stilted. It didn't help matters that the author seems to be a fan of using exclamatory sentences...a lot...and it just doesn't feel natural. I liked Rayvan and Ananais but outside of those two I didn't really care about any of the other characters. And, oy, don't even get me started on the ridiculousness of the romance <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[between Tenaka (who is no Druss IMO) and Renya <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Just...cringeworthy. I can't, in all fairness, rate this any higher than two stars.</span>

  <span id="freeText11939861858655949037" style="display:none">The journey down memory lane continues with the re-reading of David Gemmell's second instalment.<br /><br />It was fortold that there were three: Gold, Ice and Shadow.<br /><br />Reading this many years later makes me realise how memorable some of these characters were.   <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tejus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tejus" href="/user/show/2394243-tejus">Tejus</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer58829826&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer58829826" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12517674804116156844">"The King Beyond the Gate" is the sequel novel to Gemmell's first book "Legend".<br/>The story takes place around 100 years after the events of Legend. The books main focus is the character, Tenaka Khan. In "Legend", 2 main nations had been established, The Drenai, an almost western medieval society, and the Nadir. The Nadir were a bunch of individual tribes based loosely on Mongolian culture, who were united by one man - Ulric Khan. The Drenai were led by Regnak - the 2nd Earl of Bronze.<br/>Tenaka Khan </span>
  <span id="freeText12517674804116156844" style="display:none">"The King Beyond the Gate" is the sequel novel to Gemmell's first book "Legend".<br />The story takes place around 100 years after the events of Legend. The books main focus is the character, Tenaka Khan. In "Legend", 2 main nations had been established, The Drenai, an almost western medieval society, and the Nadir. The Nadir were a bunch of individual tribes based loosely on Mongolian culture, who were united by one man - Ulric Khan. The Drenai were led by Regnak - the 2nd Earl of Bronze.<br />Tenaka Khan is the great-grandson of both Regnak and Ulric. Because of his heritage, he is neither accepted by his Nadir tribesman or his Drenai Kinsmen. He eventually joins an elite Drenai mercenary force called 'The Dragon'.<br />The rest of the story deals with Tenaka after leaving the army, and having to deal with an Emperor gone mad. Its a book about self-discovery and about Tenaka finally finding peace within himself.<br />The character of Tenaka is extrememly well-written, and you find yourself rooting for this character regardless of the choices he makes.<br />There are some great action sequences as well as some comical moments. Both Legend and King Beyond the Gate are well worth checking out</span>
  <a data-text-id="12517674804116156844" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1249426461" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1249426461?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob Thompson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob Thompson" href="/user/show/4722985-rob-thompson">Rob Thompson</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4722985-rob-thompson?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4722985-rob-thompson?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4722985-rob-thompson?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1249426461" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11355772936103038212">Published in 1985 The King Beyond The Gate is the second book by Gemmell, after Legend. While the book is set in the same world it’s not a direct sequel. Many years have passed and all the previous characters are long since dead. My first impression was that this decision to set the novel so far into the future helped to give the book more of an epic feel. It was a tale that spanned generations. I also felt that Gemmells writing had improved.<br/><br/>The plot is like Legend, as are the characters. As wit</span>
  <span id="freeText11355772936103038212" style="display:none">Published in 1985 The King Beyond The Gate is the second book by Gemmell, after Legend. While the book is set in the same world it’s not a direct sequel. Many years have passed and all the previous characters are long since dead. My first impression was that this decision to set the novel so far into the future helped to give the book more of an epic feel. It was a tale that spanned generations. I also felt that Gemmells writing had improved.<br /><br />The plot is like Legend, as are the characters. As with Gemmell’s previous book one of the main themes in The King Beyond The Gate is how the main protagonists manage to survive. Especially as they are all past their physical prime. They are each haunted by their past. Gemmell does a fine job in familiarising the reader with the details of their own internal conflicts, hopes and fears.<br /><br />Being a Gemmell book you get the obligatory gore and blood. He is one of the best authors I’ve read for writing heroic combat and battle scenes. And of course these are always against overwhelming odds. He also weaves in misfortune, heartbreak, friendship, love and sorcery too.<br /><br />Mentioning sorcery, one of my minor criticisms with The King Beyond The Gate is that it uses magic more than other instalments in the series. I would have also preferred to hear about how the Dragon had fallen and Ceska rose to power at the start of the book too. As this doesn't happen, at the start of the book we get the main characters bumping into one another by chance. I felt at this point the plotting could have been somewhat tighter.<br /><br />So in summary, I’d recommend The King Beyond The Gate if you love exciting action driven fantasy novels. Perhaps not my favourite Gemmell book but The King Beyond The Gate does what is says on the tin: it doesn’t try to be any more than enjoyable entertainment.<br /><br /><b>Quotes</b><br /><br />As with all Gemmell books, I love to pick out the quotes which resonated with me. Here are the ones I highlighted when reading The King Beyond The Gate:<br /><br />- Too many people go through life without pausing to enjoy what they have. /Ch. 2<br />- Nothing in life is sure, my son. Except the promise of death. /Ch. 4<br />- Evil lives in a pit. If you want to fight it, you must climb down into the slime to do so. White cloaks show the dirt more thank black, and silver tarnishes. /Ch. 10<br />- All things in the world are created for man, yet all have two purposes. The waters run that we might drink of them, but they are also symbols of the futility of man. They reflect our lives in rushing beauty, birthed in the purity of the mountains. As babes they babble and run, gushing and growing as they mature into strong young rivers. Then they widen and slow until at least they meander, like old men, to join with the sea. /Ch. 12<br />- "Foolish: It's all foolish. Life is a farce— a stupid, sickening farce played out by fools." /Ch. 16<br />- "I had a teacher ... He said there were three kinds of people in life: winners, losers and fighters. Winners made him sick with their arrogance, losers made him sick with their whining, and fighters made him sick with their stupidity." "In which category did he put himself?" "He said he had tried all three and nothing suited him." "Well, at least he tried. That's all a man can do, Lake. And we shall try." / Ch. 19<br />- A man makes mistakes, but he lives by them. Foolish it may be on occasion. But in the main it is the only way to live. We are what we say only so long as our words are iron. /Ch. 19<br />- All things are possible, ... Except the passing of regret. /Ch. 20<br />- Life is sad enough, Magir. Laughter is a thing to be treasured. /Ch. 22</span>
  <a data-text-id="11355772936103038212" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_30393406" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/30393406" />
    <a title="Tracey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/841949-tracey"><img alt="Tracey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325394892p2/841949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/30393406?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tracey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tracey" href="/user/show/841949-tracey">Tracey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345379054" href="/book/show/544619.The_King_Beyond_the_Gate">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/841949-tracey?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/841949-tracey?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/841949-tracey?shelf=mercenaries">mercenaries</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer30393406" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10064929062387292445">I reread Legend for a group read, wanted to keep going… Another book, another siege. I hesitate to say this, but here goes: these first three books of the Chronicles of the Drenai tend to blur together a bit for me. It's true <i>The King Beyond the Gate</i>'s Tenaka Khan is very different from Waylander in some ways - but not in others; Waylander was in turn in some ways (though not others) strongly reminiscent of Druss. The overarching plotlines were different, the allies and enemies different, but … </span>
  <span id="freeText10064929062387292445" style="display:none">I reread Legend for a group read, wanted to keep going… Another book, another siege. I hesitate to say this, but here goes: these first three books of the Chronicles of the Drenai tend to blur together a bit for me. It's true <i>The King Beyond the Gate</i>'s Tenaka Khan is very different from Waylander in some ways - but not in others; Waylander was in turn in some ways (though not others) strongly reminiscent of Druss. The overarching plotlines were different, the allies and enemies different, but … Here are more ruined fortresses and pillaged villages, more they-can-never-win battles, more insuperable opponents, and another monstrous body count. For me it did not pay to read the books back-to-back; the time jumps between stories were too disconcerting, especially with the connecting thread of the Armor of Bronze. The formula is so strong and, after two books, familiar that the occasional jaunts away from that formula were disorienting. (The worst of both worlds, that.)<br /> <br />Also, while the writing was still strong and spare and good, this time around I noticed some words that caused a bit of a jolt: i.e, e.g.: “ricochet” (the etymology for which is from the French (of course), in the later 1700's). (It isn’t a good example, but I didn’t make note of others; there might have been examples in the other books which I simply never registered.) I've ranted before about the use of inappropriate language (in terms of anachronisms and words too readily identified with their original language, not in terms of profanity), and the Drenai books didn't push me to the level of ranting; it was merely that there were occasional words used which gave me a small bump out of the story and the world it was set in: <i>they don't have French there</i> or <i>they shouldn't be aware of that concept</i>.<br /> <br />There is a strong division between black and white in the Drenai Tales: the bad guys kill little girls, the good guys grow roses. And it’s literal: you have the shining silver Thirty and the black-clad Hounds. And in between, a conflicted “hero”, or anti-hero – or a hero without internal conflict so much as herded by fate somewhere he would never have chosen to go. It was very strange to read about a half-Nadir main character, having finished <i>Legend</i> just before reading this; still, he's a good character, and the internal codes are not violated because nearly everyone in the book hates Tenaka Khan, Drenai and Nadir alike. <br /> <br />The Joinings were another source of unease for me – apart from the obvious reasons, I mean. Yes, they're horrible creatures, especially once you're given the background of exactly what they are; but that's not what I was thinking of. They are introduced early in the book, and are such a drastic departure from everything that has gone before that I was taken aback. It took quite a while to come to the explanation for them.<br /> <br />I'll continue on with the series after a while – I think I'll benefit from a break. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10064929062387292445" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12712856370689512434">Vote: 3,25<br/>Class: L-B2 (FP)<br/><br/>I was positively impressed by the first book of the Drenai Saga (The Legend). It captivated me.<br/>I pinpointed some shortcomings of that book but I really hoped that they would be addressed by The King Beyond the Gate.<br/>Well, they weren't.   <span id="freeText12712856370689512434" style="display:none">Vote: 3,25<br />Class: L-B2 (FP)<br /><br />I was positively impressed by the first book of the Drenai Saga (The Legend). It captivated me.<br />I pinpointed some shortcomings of that book but I really hoped that they would be addressed by The King Beyond the Gate.<br />Well, they weren't. It's a good book, not an awesome one.<br /><br />The World (2,50) is the same of the first book and it lacks too many details about its history, its geografy, and its languages. They can't all simply speak the same language, you can't tell me of some machines they found of a lost past. What past? Why lost? How they were discovered? And so on.<br /><br />The characters (3.50) are good. They will win you. Some others are a bit too shallow.<br /><br />The plot (3,00) is (almost) good. The only thing is that it seems an episode disconnected from the story of the World: it didn't leave anything behind.<br /><br />The style (4.00) is very nice and smooth.<br /><br />Overall you can say: a good fantasy book, if you don't know what to read, you can read it but do not expect anything extraordinary.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12712856370689512434" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText18367499004975493008" style="display:none">Its David Gemmell so his writing and plotting are as good as ever. All his books are incredibly readable, incredibly full and never milk their history. As ever there are hundreds of tales within this you would like to know more about but never will. I thought the ending was well realised and very interesting and yet rang true.<br /><br />Magnificently done. If you like fantasy and have never read a David Gemmell book then you are missing a treat. Try any of them now.</span>

<div id="review_2194599607" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2194599607" />
    <a title="Pallav" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6023649-pallav"><img alt="Pallav" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461002234p2/6023649.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2194599607?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pallav" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pallav" href="/user/show/6023649-pallav">Pallav</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2194599607" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9076077125236598790">The story about how the Drenai books came to be is pretty interesting. Gemmell was diagnosed with cancer and he wrote the first book Legend as a way to deal with his own mortality, to come to terms with it. But, as he finished the book, his cancer went into remission. He'd already published the book or maybe sent it for publishing, so he decided to write book 2. The rest is history!<br/><br/>This book goes way in future as compared to the first book. There are descendants of the dudes from the first book </span>
  <span id="freeText9076077125236598790" style="display:none">The story about how the Drenai books came to be is pretty interesting. Gemmell was diagnosed with cancer and he wrote the first book Legend as a way to deal with his own mortality, to come to terms with it. But, as he finished the book, his cancer went into remission. He'd already published the book or maybe sent it for publishing, so he decided to write book 2. The rest is history!<br /><br />This book goes way in future as compared to the first book. There are descendants of the dudes from the first book in this one and there is the similar premise of a small group facing impossible odds. I liked a few things about this book such as the pacing, the cast of varied characters, the last stands, the evil dude was a paper-thin character, and I was not really clear about his motivations till the end, but the efforts, the bravery, and the sacrifice of the characters in the book were all amazing and more than amazing. <br /><br />A simple book, won't leave you with much food for thought, a linear story, but you can get done in a few hours, so there is that. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9076077125236598790" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7509315610820034414" style="display:none">4 Stars<br /><br />I have really enjoyed revisiting this book/series. My reading buddy hadn’t read the series before, but has also enjoyed discovering David Gemmell’s work/s.<br /></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IIyyPea0+dnLKqUx4M0S6xkpQb4F+A29OBj0zL3hvMEOK2RSXyokKCdZpCulSUzmIn5snU9a06YPTrDHKRjbUA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('LEUuyjylwIcXYAlVyGCMwlY3pj1/Arv5E1Y47PJeDUYC4vilhTsddvsTCE+N5NLPbWCLHjWgZeIkAHznZqdq1w==')})
  }

New York Times bestselling fantasist Raymond E. Feist returns to a beleaguered realm of wonders and magic-where war is an enduring legacy; where blood swells the rivers and nourishes the land. Attend to this hitherto untold chapter in the violent history of Midkemia -- a towering saga of great conflicts, brave acts and insidious intrigues. It is the story of a traitor who rejects the brutality of his warlike kind and casts his lot with the human targets of their fierce aggression. It tells of mysterious deaths and sinister machinations -- and signs of a time when the fate of many civilizations rested in the able, unfaltering hands of RiftWar veterans Squire Locklear and cunning their-turned-squire Jimmy the Hand. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5326779288774618728">David Andrew Gemmell was a bestselling British author of heroic fantasy. A former journalist and newspaper editor, Gemmell had his first work of fiction published in 1984. He went on to write over thirty novels. Best known for his debut, Legend, Gemmell's works display violence, yet also explores themes in honour, loyalty and redemption. With over one million copies sold, his work continues to sel</span>
  <span id="freeText5326779288774618728" style="display:none">David Andrew Gemmell was a bestselling British author of heroic fantasy. A former journalist and newspaper editor, Gemmell had his first work of fiction published in 1984. He went on to write over thirty novels. Best known for his debut, Legend, Gemmell's works display violence, yet also explores themes in honour, loyalty and redemption. With over one million copies sold, his work continues to sell worldwide.</span>
